\\\\"SaaS Multiples 2025 Complete Guide to Valuation Metrics and Benchmarks Flippa.com\\\\")\\\\n\\\\nSaaS multiples are critical tools for valuing software-as-a-service businesses. They simplify complex financial data into actionable benchmarks, helping you understand where your business stands and how it compares to others in the market. In 2025, SaaS valuation has become more important than ever, with the global SaaS market projected to hit $390 billion this year and continue its rapid growth.\\\\n\\\\nWhether you plan to sell your [SaaS business](https://flippa.com/buy/sitetype/saas), attract investors, or simply measure your company\\\\u2019s performance, knowing how SaaS multiples work is essential. Focusing on key metrics like recurring revenue, profitability, and customer retention, these multiples help translate your business\\\\u2019s potential into tangible value. This guide breaks down everything you need to know about SaaS multiples and metrics so you can confidently navigate the valuation process.\\\\n\\\\n## Key Takeaways\\\\n\\\\n* **SaaS multiples** are used to value software businesses by comparing financial metrics like **revenue**, **ARR**, and **profitability** to the **company\\\\u2019s valuation**.\\\\n* In 2025, factors like **ARR growth**, **customer retention**, and **market trends** are key to securing higher multiples, typically **ranging from 3x\\\\u201310x ARR** for private companies **and 7x\\\\u201312x** for public ones.\\\\n* To boost valuation, focus on **growth**, **reduce churn**, **improve efficiency**, and **showcase your unique strengths**. They work by dividing a company\\\\u2019s valuation by specific metrics like revenue or profitability. Understanding these multiples provides a clearer picture of your business\\\\u2019s market value and potential.\\\\n\\\\nLet\\\\u2019s break down the most common SaaS multiples and how they\\\\u2019re calculated.\\\\n\\\\n ![saas valuation methods](data:image/svg+xml...) ![saas valuation methods](https://flippa.com/blog/wp-content/uploads/2025/09/saas-valuation-methods-1.svg)\\\\n\\\\n### Revenue Multiple\\\\n\\\\nThe revenue multiple compares your company\\\\u2019s total revenue to its valuation. It\\\\u2019s one of the simplest ways to measure value, especially for high-growth SaaS companies focusing on expanding their customer base.\\\\n\\\\n**Formula:**Revenue Multiple = [Business Valuation](https://flippa.com/blog/how-to-sell-a-business/) \\\\u00f7 Total Revenue\\\\n\\\\n**Example:**\\\\n\\\\nA SaaS business generates $2 million in annual revenue and has a valuation of $10 million.\\\\n\\\\nThe revenue multiple is: *10,000,000 \\\\u00f7 2,000,000 = 5x*\\\\n\\\\n### ARR Multiple\\\\n\\\\nThe annual recurring revenue (ARR) multiple focuses on the most important revenue stream for SaaS businesses: subscription revenue. Since ARR represents predictable, recurring income, it\\\\u2019s a key metric for SaaS investors.\\\\n\\\\n**Formula:**ARR Multiple = Business Valuation \\\\u00f7 ARR\\\\n\\\\n**Example:**\\\\n\\\\nA SaaS company with a $5 million ARR and a valuation of $35 million.\\\\n\\\\nThe ARR multiple is: *35,000,000 \\\\u00f7 5,000,000 = 7x*\\\\n\\\\n### EBITDA Multiple\\\\n\\\\nThe EBITDA (Earnings Before Interest, Taxes, Depreciation, and Amortization) multiple focuses on a company\\\\u2019s profitability. It\\\\u2019s commonly used for more established SaaS businesses that are generating steady profits.\\\\n\\\\n**Formula:**EBITDA Multiple = Business Valuation \\\\u00f7 EBITDA\\\\n\\\\n**Example:**\\\\n\\\\nA SaaS company with $3 million EBITDA and a valuation of $18 million.\\\\n\\\\nThe estimated EBITDA multiple is: *18,000,000 \\\\u00f7 3,000,000 = 6x*\\\\n\\\\n### Gross Margin Multiple\\\\n\\\\nThe gross margin multiple highlights how efficiently your business generates revenue compared to its costs. SaaS businesses with high gross margins (often above 75%) tend to attract higher valuations.\\\\n\\\\n**Formula:**Gross Margin Multiple = Business Valuation \\\\u00f7 Gross Margin\\\\n\\\\n**Example:**\\\\n\\\\nIf your gross margin is $8 million and your company is valued at $40 million.\\\\n\\\\nYour gross margin SaaS valuation multiple is: *40,000,000 \\\\u00f7 8,000,000 = 5x*\\\\n\\\\n### Net Revenue Retention (NRR) Multiple\\\\n\\\\nNet Revenue Retention (NRR) measures your ability to retain and grow revenue from existing customers. A high NRR indicates strong customer satisfaction and successful upselling.\\\\n\\\\n**Formula:**NRR = (Starting ARR + Upsells \\\\u2013 Churned Revenue) \\\\u00f7 Starting ARR\\\\n\\\\n**Example:** A company starts with $10 million ARR, gains $3 million from upsells, and loses $1 million to churn.\\\\n\\\\nThe NRR is: *(10,000,000 + 3,000,000 \\\\u2013 1,000,000) \\\\u00f7 10,000,000 = 120%*\\\\n\\\\n### Monthly Recurring Revenue (MRR) Multiple\\\\n\\\\nThe MRR multiple evaluates short-term recurring revenue, offering a snapshot of your company\\\\u2019s immediate performance. It\\\\u2019s often used for smaller SaaS businesses or those in earlier stages.\\\\n\\\\n**Formula:**MRR Multiple = Business Valuation \\\\u00f7 MRR\\\\n\\\\n**Example:** A company with $200,000 in MRR and a valuation of $2.4 million.\\\\n\\\\nThe MRR multiple of this company would be: *2,400,000 \\\\u00f7 200,000 = 12x*\\\\n\\\\n**Making It Easy to Sell Online Businesses**Flippa provides owners and investors with the tools and expertise to sell\\\\n\\\\n\\\\u2714\\\\ufe0f 400,000+ Weekly Active Buyers\\\\n\\\\n\\\\u2714\\\\ufe0f 20+ Multi-Language Brokers\\\\n\\\\n\\\\u2714\\\\ufe0f Negotiate and Receive Offers Fast\\\\n\\\\n\\\\u2714\\\\ufe0f Integrated Legal, Insurance and Payments\\\\n\\\\n[Get a Free Valuation](https://flippa.com/free-valuation?buy_sell=Blog_Blog_Post_Valuation)\\\\n[Sell Now](https://flippa.com/sell?buy_sell=Blog)\\\\n\\\\n## How the Rule of 40 Impacts SaaS Multiples\\\\n\\\\nOne of the most important valuation signals in SaaS is the **Rule of 40**, the idea that a healthy SaaS business should have a combined **growth rate and profit margin of at least 40%**. For example, a business growing at 30% annually with a 10% EBITDA margin would meet this threshold.\\\\n\\\\nIn 2025, investors are paying close attention to this metric as the market shifts from growth-at-all-costs to sustainable, profitable expansion. Companies exceeding the Rule of 40 consistently command higher EV/ARR multiples; often **2x to 3x higher** than peers with weak margins or declining growth.\\\\n\\\\n**If you want to increase your SaaS multiple, focus on:**\\\\n\\\\n* Reducing churn\\\\n* Improving gross margin\\\\n* Reinvesting profitably in growth\\\\n\\\\nThe Rule of 40 acts as a shortcut for buyers to assess efficiency and long-term viability, especially for businesses in the $500K\\\\u2014$5M valuation range.\\\\n\\\\n ![how to increase saas multiples](data:image/svg+xml...) ![how to increase saas multiples](https://flippa.com/blog/wp-content/uploads/2025/09/how-to-increase-saas-multiples.svg)\\\\n\\\\n## Why do SaaS Multiples Matter so Much?\\\\n\\\\nSaaS multiples give you a clear way to measure your company\\\\u2019s value. Whether you\\\\u2019re selling, raising funds, or just benchmarking your business, these numbers help you see where you stand. Higher multiples usually mean strong growth and solid financials, while lower ones can highlight areas to improve.\\\\n\\\\n***\\\\u201cUnderstanding SaaS multiples is key to navigating the valuation process, whether you\\\\u2019re preparing for a sale or attracting investors,\\\\u201d*** **says** [**Blake Hutchison, CEO of Flippa**](https://flippa.com/blog/author/blake-hutchison/)**.** ***\\\\u201cThe right metrics not only tell a compelling story about your business but also position it effectively in a competitive marketplace.\\\\u201d***\\\\n\\\\nMultiples also let investors and [SaaS buyers](https://flippa.com/blog/buying-a-saas-business-the-complete-guide-to-due-diligence/) compare businesses quickly. You\\\\u2019re more likely to secure a better valuation if your company has strong ARR growth, low churn, and efficient operations. Knowing how to interpret and improve these metrics gives you an edge when it\\\\u2019s time to make big moves.\\\\n\\\\n## Key Factors That Affect SaaS Multiples\\\\n\\\\nSeveral factors directly influence how a business is valued when evaluating SaaS multiples. These factors highlight a company\\\\u2019s growth potential, operational efficiency, and customer loyalty, which are crucial for attracting premium valuations.\\\\n\\\\n ![saas valuation biggest impact](data:image/svg+xml...) ![saas valuation biggest impact](https://flippa.com/blog/wp-content/uploads/2025/09/saas-valuation-biggest-impact.svg)\\\\n\\\\n### ARR Growth Rate\\\\n\\\\nARR growth is one of the most significant drivers of SaaS multiples. Businesses growing their ARR at 40% or more annually tend to secure premium valuations, as this growth signals strong demand and scalability.\\\\n\\\\n### Churn Rate\\\\n\\\\nThe churn rate measures the percentage of customers who cancel their subscriptions over a given period. Lower churn rates (typically under 10%) indicate strong customer retention and satisfaction, directly supporting recurring revenue stability.\\\\n\\\\n### Profit Margins\\\\n\\\\nProfitability plays a key role in valuation. SaaS businesses with EBITDA margins over 20% are often seen as efficient and financially stable, making them attractive to buyers. Conversely, companies with negative EBITDA but high growth may still achieve strong valuations in high-demand markets.\\\\n\\\\n### Customer Acquisition Cost (CAC)\\\\n\\\\nEfficient CAC management reflects a company\\\\u2019s ability to acquire customers cost-effectively. A favorable CAC to customer lifetime value (LTV) ratio of 1:3 or better shows that a business is acquiring customers efficiently and generating significant value from them.\\\\n\\\\n### Market Trends\\\\n\\\\nSaaS businesses operating in high-growth sectors like AI, cybersecurity, or healthcare often command premium multiples. These industries benefit from sustained demand and innovation, making them particularly appealing to investors.\\\\n\\\\n**Making It Easy to Sell Online Businesses**Flippa provides owners and investors with the tools and expertise to sell\\\\n\\\\n\\\\u2714\\\\ufe0f 400,000+ Weekly Active Buyers\\\\n\\\\n\\\\u2714\\\\ufe0f 20+ Multi-Language Brokers\\\\n\\\\n\\\\u2714\\\\ufe0f Negotiate and Receive Offers Fast\\\\n\\\\n\\\\u2714\\\\ufe0f Integrated Legal, Insurance and Payments\\\\n\\\\n[Get a Free Valuation](https://flippa.com/free-valuation?buy_sell=Blog_Blog_Post_Valuation)\\\\n[Sell Now](https://flippa.com/sell?buy_sell=Blog)\\\\n\\\\n## SaaS Valuation Benchmarks for 2025\\\\n\\\\nUnderstanding SaaS valuation benchmarks is key for anyone looking to assess or enhance the value of a SaaS business. Here\\\\u2019s a breakdown of the expected multiples for 2025:\\\\n\\\\n ![saas multiples by growth rate](data:image/svg+xml...) ![saas multiples by growth rate](https://flippa.com/blog/wp-content/uploads/2025/09/saas-multiples-by-growth-rate.svg)\\\\n\\\\n### Private SaaS Companies\\\\n\\\\n* **Low Growth (<20% ARR Growth):** Valuation multiples for private SaaS companies with ARR growth below 20% typically range from **3x to 5x ARR**.\\\\n* **Moderate Growth (20-40% ARR Growth):** Companies experiencing moderate growth can expect multiples between **5x to 7x ARR**.\\\\n* **High Growth (>40% ARR Growth):** High-growth private SaaS firms boasting ARR growth exceeding 40% may achieve multiples ranging from **7x to 10x ARR**.\\\\n\\\\n### Public SaaS Companies\\\\n\\\\n* **Median Multiples:** Publicly traded SaaS companies generally exhibit valuation multiples averaging between **7x to 8x ARR**.\\\\n* **Top Performers:** Leading public SaaS companies with exceptional growth and profitability can attain multiples exceeding **10x ARR**, reflecting strong investor confidence and market leadership.\\\\n\\\\n### Global Variations in Multiples\\\\n\\\\n* **North America:** Typically higher multiples (8x to 15x ARR) due to market maturity.\\\\n* **Europe:** Multiples average between 5x and 10x ARR.\\\\n* **Asia-Pacific:** Emerging markets see 4x to 8x ARR with growth potential.\\\\n\\\\n## SaaS Multiples by Industry\\\\n\\\\nBeyond deal size, industry can have a significant impact on valuation. Profit multiples surged in 2022, driven by optimism for high-growth SaaS companies, with the top decile reaching impressive highs. However, they cooled in 2023 amid economic tightening before stabilizing at moderate levels in 2024 as market confidence rebounded.\\\\n\\\\n ![](data:image/svg+xml...) ![](https://flippa.com/blog/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/flippa-historical-data-1-1024x683.jpg)\\\\n\\\\nRevenue multiples followed a similar trajectory. They peaked in early 2022, fueled by strong investor interest in SaaS businesses during a period of accelerated digital adoption. By 2023, these multiples declined as the focus shifted to profitability over growth. In 2024, revenue multiples showed modest recovery, reflecting improvements in market dynamics and the increasing adoption of AI-powered SaaS solutions.\\\\n\\\\n ![](data:image/svg+xml...) ![](https://flippa.com/blog/wp-content/uploads/2025/08/flippa-historical-data-2-1024x683.jpg)\\\\n\\\\nThese trends demonstrate a shift in investor preferences from pure growth to sustainable profitability and operational efficiency. As SaaS companies prepare for 2025, businesses with strong financial fundamentals and growth potential will likely command premium multiples.\\\\n\\\\n## How to Maximize SaaS Multiples\\\\n\\\\nAchieving higher SaaS multiples requires a combination of strong financial performance, efficient operations, and strategic market positioning. Cut unnecessary costs and use automation tools to reduce manual processes. These actions improve profit margins, making your business more appealing to investors or buyers.\\\\n\\\\n### Highlight Competitive Advantages\\\\n\\\\nDemonstrate how your product stands out. Highlighting your niche dominance or innovative features ensures your business is seen as a market leader.\\\\n\\\\n### Diversify Revenue Streams\\\\n\\\\nMultiple revenue streams reduce risk and enhance stability. Offer tiered pricing to attract different customer segments, introduce add-on services to boost income, and create enterprise-level packages for high-value clients. This diversification strengthens your overall revenue mix.\\\\n\\\\n### Build Scalable Customer Acquisition\\\\n\\\\nA scalable acquisition strategy is key to growth. Maintain a strong CAC-to-LTV ratio, ideally 1:3 or better, to demonstrate efficient customer acquisition. Diversify your channels; combine organic, paid, and referral efforts, to ensure consistent growth without over-relying on one source.\\\\n\\\\n### Use Professional Tools\\\\n\\\\nUsing the right tools can make a big difference in maximizing your SaaS valuation. This business was built on a scalable subscription model with strong recurring revenue, demonstrating many key factors influencing SaaS multiples.\\\\n\\\\nThe company\\\\u2019s value was driven by:\\\\n\\\\n* **Recurring Revenue & ARR Growth:** With predictable revenue streams from a subscription-based model, the business attracted buyer interest and secured a competitive valuation.\\\\n* **Profitability & Operational Efficiency:** Unlike early-stage SaaS startups prioritizing growth over profits, this business had a strong EBITDA margin, making it more appealing to investors looking for a steady return.\\\\n* **Customer Retention & Low Churn:** High renewal rates and strong customer engagement contributed to a higher valuation multiple as buyers look for businesses with predictable revenue streams.\\\\n\\\\nWhile every SaaS business is unique, this case study shows how strong financials and solid business fundamentals can directly impact valuation. Take the steps today to understand your business\\\\u2019s true value and set yourself up for long-term success.\\\\n\\\\n## FAQs\\\\n\\\\n### What is a SaaS multiple, and how is it calculated?\\\\n\\\\nA SaaS multiple is a valuation metric that compares a company\\\\u2019s value to a specific financial measure, such as ARR, EBITDA, or revenue. It\\\\u2019s calculated by dividing the company\\\\u2019s valuation by the chosen metric.\\\\n\\\\n### What influences SaaS multiples the most?\\\\n\\\\nKey factors include ARR growth, churn rate, profitability, and market trends. High-growth companies with strong retention rates and efficient customer acquisition often command premium multiples.\\\\n\\\\n### What\\\\u2019s the difference between public and private SaaS multiples?\\\\n\\\\nPublic SaaS companies generally achieve higher multiples (8x\\\\u201312x ARR on average) due to greater market visibility and investor confidence. Private SaaS companies often range from 3x\\\\u2013to 8x ARR, as they carry higher perceived risks, including limited [liquidity](https://flippa.com/blog/dictionary/what-is-liquidity/) and smaller market footprints.\\\\n\\\\n### How can I improve my SaaS multiple?\\\\n\\\\nFocus on metrics like ARR growth, NRR, and LTV. specialized AI agents\n"""\n\nfrom abc import ABC, abstractmethod\nfrom typing import Dict, Any, List, Optional\nfrom datetime import datetime\nfrom enum import Enum\nimport asyncio\nimport json\n\n\nclass AgentType(Enum):\n    """Types of specialized agents"""\n    CODING = "coding"\n    RESEARCH = "research"\n    WRITING = "writing"\n    IMAGE = "image"\n    DATA_ANALYSIS = "data_analysis"\n    DEBUGGING = "debugging"\n    TESTING = "testing"\n    DOCUMENTATION = "documentation"\n\n\nclass AgentCapability(Enum):\n    """Agent capabilities"""\n    CODE_GENERATION = "code_generation"\n    CODE_REVIEW = "code_review"\n    BUG_FIXING = "bug_fixing"\n    REFACTORING = "refactoring"\n    TESTING = "testing"\n    DOCUMENTATION = "documentation"\n    RESEARCH = "research"\n    WRITING = "writing"\n    IMAGE_GENERATION = "image_generation"\n    IMAGE_ANALYSIS = "image_analysis"\n    DATA_ANALYSIS = "data_analysis"\n    WEB_SCRAPING = "web_scraping"\n\n\nclass TaskPriority(Enum):\n    """Task priority levels"""\n    LOW = 1\n    MEDIUM = 2\n    HIGH = 3\n    CRITICAL = 4\n\n\nclass TaskStatus(Enum):\n    """Task execution status"""\n    PENDING = "pending"\n    IN_PROGRESS = "in_progress"\n    COMPLETED = "completed"\n    FAILED = "failed"\n    CANCELLED = "cancelled"\n\n\nclass AgentTask:\n    """Represents a task for an agent"""\n    \n    def __init__(\n        self,\n        task_id: str,\n        description: str,\n        priority: TaskPriority = TaskPriority.MEDIUM,\n        context: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None,\n        metadata: Optional[Dict[str, Any]] = None\n    ):\n        self.task_id = task_id\n        self.description = description\n        self.priority = priority\n        self.context = context or {}\n        self.metadata = metadata or {}\n        self.status = TaskStatus.PENDING\n        self.created_at = datetime.utcnow()\n        self.started_at: Optional[datetime] = None\n        self.completed_at: Optional[datetime] = None\n        self.result: Optional[Any] = None\n        self.error: Optional[str] = None\n        self.subtasks: List[\'AgentTask\'] = []\n        \n    def to_dict(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:\n        """Convert task to dictionary"""\n        return {\n            "task_id": self.task_id,\n            "description": self.description,\n            "priority": self.priority.value,\n            "status": self.status.value,\n            "context": self.context,\n            "metadata": self.metadata,\n            "created_at": self.created_at.isoformat(),\n            "started_at": self.started_at.isoformat() if self.started_at else None,\n            "completed_at": self.completed_at.isoformat() if self.completed_at else None,\n            "result": self.result,\n            "error": self.error,\n            "subtasks": [st.to_dict() for st in self.subtasks]\n        }\n\n\nclass BaseAgent(ABC):\n    """\n    Base class for all specialized AI agents\n    \n    Provides common functionality:\n    - Task management\n    - Context handling\n    - Model selection\n    - Error handling\n    - Logging\n    """\n    \n    def __init__(\n        self,\n        agent_type: AgentType,\n        name: str,\n        description: str,\n        capabilities: List[AgentCapability],\n        preferred_models: Optional[List[str]] = None\n    ):\n        self.agent_type = agent_type\n        self.name = name\n        self.description = description\n        self.capabilities = capabilities\n        self.preferred_models = preferred_models or ["gpt-4o", "claude-3.5-sonnet"]\n        self.tasks: Dict[str, AgentTask] = {}\n        self.context_memory: Dict[str, Any] = {}\n        self.is_busy = False\n        \n    @abstractmethod\n    async def execute_task(self, task: AgentTask) -> Any:\n        """\n        Execute a task\n        Must be implemented by subclasses\n        """\n        pass\n    \n    @abstractmethod\n    async def can_handle(self, task_description: str) -> bool:\n        """\n        Check if agent can handle a task\n        Must be implemented by subclasses\n        """\n        pass\n    \n    async def process_task(self, task: AgentTask) -> Dict[str, Any]:\n        """\n        Process a task with full lifecycle management\n        """\n        try:\n            # Update task status\n            task.status = TaskStatus.IN_PROGRESS\n            task.started_at = datetime.utcnow()\n            self.is_busy = True\n            \n            # Break down into subtasks if needed\n            subtasks = await self.break_down_task(task)\n            if subtasks:\n                task.subtasks = subtasks\n                # Execute subtasks\n                subtask_results = []\n                for subtask in subtasks:\n                    result = await self.execute_task(subtask)\n                    subtask_results.append(result)\n                # Compile results\n                task.result = await self.compile_results(subtask_results)\n            else:\n                # Execute task directly\n                task.result = await self.execute_task(task)\n            \n            # Update task status\n            task.status = TaskStatus.COMPLETED\n            task.completed_at = datetime.utcnow()\n            \n            # Store in context memory\n            self.store_in_memory(task)\n            \n            return {\n                "success": True,\n                "task_id": task.task_id,\n                "result": task.result,\n                "execution_time": (task.completed_at - task.started_at).total_seconds()\n            }\n            \n        except Exception as e:\n            task.status = TaskStatus.FAILED\n            task.error = str(e)\n            task.completed_at = datetime.utcnow()\n            \n            return {\n                "success": False,\n                "task_id": task.task_id,\n                "error": str(e)\n            }\n        finally:\n            self.is_busy = False\n    \n    async def break_down_task(self, task: AgentTask) -> List[AgentTask]:\n        """\n        Break down \n    async def _execute_task(self, task: Task, worker_id: int):\n        """Execute a task"""\n        task.status = TaskStatus.IN_PROGRESS\n        task.started_at = datetime.utcnow()\n     self.completed_tasks[task.task_id] = task_result\n            \n            # Execute callbacks\n            await self._execute_callbacks(task.task_id, task_result)\n            \n after {task.timeout} seconds"\n            await self._handle_task_failure(task)\n            \n        except Exception as e:\n            task.status = TaskStatus.FAILED\n            task.error = async def _handle_task_failure(self, task: Task):\n        """Handle task failure with retry logic"""\n        logger.error(f"Task failed: {task.task_id} ({task.name}) - {task.error}")\n        \n        # Retry if possible\n        if task.retry_count < task.max_retries:\n            task.retry_count += 1\n            task.status = TaskStatus.QUEUED\n            await self.queue.put((task.priority.value, task.task_id))\n            logger.info(f"Retrying task: {task.task_id} (attempt {task.retry_count}/{task.max_retries})")\n        else:\n            # Max retries task.started_at).total_seconds() if task.started_at else 0,\n                metadata=task.metadata\n            )\n            \n            self.completed_tasks[task.task_id] = task_result\n            \n            # Execute callbacks\n            await self._execute_callbacks(task.task_id, task_result)\n    \n    async def _execute_callbacks(self, task_id: str, result: TaskResult):\n        """Execute registered callbacks"""\n        if task_id in self.callbacks:\n            for callback in self.callbacks[task_id]:\n                try:\n                    if asyncio.iscoroutinefunction(callback):\n                        await callback(result)\n                    else:\n                        callback(result)\n                except Exception as e:\n                    logger.error(f"Callback error for task {task_id}: {str(e)}")\n    \n    async def compile_results(self, task_ids: List[str], wait: bool = True) -> Dict[str, Any]:\n        """\n        Compile results from multiple tasks\n        \n        Args:\n            task_ids: List of task IDs\n            wait: Wait for all tasks to complete\n            \n        Returns:\n            Compiled results\n        """\n        if wait:\n            # Wait for all tasks to complete\n            while not all(tid in self.completed_tasks for tid in task_ids):\n                await asyncio.sleep(0.1)\n        \n        results = []\n        errors = []\n        \n        for task_id in task_ids:\n            if task_id in self.completed_tasks:\n                result = self.completed_tasks[task_id]\n                if result.status == TaskStatus.COMPLETED:\n                    results.append(result.result)\n                else:\n                    errors.append({\n                        "task_id": task_id,\n                        "error": result.error\n                    })\n        \n        return {\n            "total_tasks": len(task_ids),\n            "completed": len(results),\n            "failed": len(errors),\n            "results": results,\n            "errors": errors\n        }\n    \n    def get_statistics(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:\n        """Get queue statistics"""\n        total_tasks = len(self.tasks) + len(self.completed_tasks)\n        completed = len([t for t in self.completed_tasks.values() if t.status == TaskStatus.COMPLETED])\n        failed = len([t for t in self.completed_tasks.values() if t.status == TaskStatus.FAILED])\n        \n        return {\n            "total_tasks": total_tasks,\n            "pending": len([t for t in self.tasks.values() if t.status == TaskStatus.PENDING]),\n            "queued": len([t for t in self.tasks.values() if t.status == TaskStatus.QUEUED]),\n            "in_progress": len(self.active_tasks),\n            "completed": completed,\n            "failed": failed,\n            "cancelled": len([t for t in self.tasks.values() if t.status == TaskStatus.CANCELLED]),\n            "success_rate": completed / total_tasks if total_tasks > 0 else 0,\n            "active_workers": len(self.workers),\n            "max_workers": self.max_workers\n        }\n\n\n# Global task queue instance\ntask_queue = TaskQueue(max_workers=5)\n</create-file>\n</function_calls>'}

File path or URL\n            if image.startswith((\'http://\', \'https://\')):\n                return image  # URL\n            else:\n                # Read file\n                with open(image, \'rb\') as f:\n                    image_bytes = f.read()\n                return base64.b64encode(image_bytes).decode(\'utf-8\')\n        \n        elif isinstance(image, bytes):\n            # Raw bytes\n            return base64.b64encode(image).decode(\'utf-8\')\n        \n        elif isinstance(image, Image.Image):\n            # PIL Image\n            buffer = io.BytesIO()\n            image.save(buffer, format=\'PNG\')\n            image_bytes = buffer.getvalue()\n            return base64.b64encode(image_bytes).decode(\'utf-8\')\n        \n        else:\n            raise ValueError(f"Unsupported image type: {type(image)}")\n    \n    def _get_task_prompt(self, task: VisionTask) -> str:\n        """Get prompt for specific task"""\n        prompts = {\n            VisionTask.GENERAL_ANALYSIS: "Analyze this image in detail.
